See Tables 1 and S2 for raw data.
###end p 48
###begin title 49
###xml 133 142 133 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 144 153 140 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 155 164 147 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 170 179 158 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
Genetic map distances (cM) and the distribution of parental and recombinant progeny for the EAY1108/EAY1112 strain background in WT, csm4Delta, ndj1Delta, msh5Delta, and mlh1Delta strains on chromosome XV.
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 57 58 57 58 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sup>
###xml 233 234 233 234 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</sup>
###xml 684 688 684 688 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Perkins1">[38]</xref>
All mutants are isogenic derivatives of EAY1108/EAY1112. aIntervals correspond to the genetic distance calculated from tetrads +/- one standard error. Standard error was calculated using the Stahl Laboratory Online Tools website (). bData shown as 95% confidence intervals around the recombination frequency determined from single spores. To facilitate comparisons to the tetrad data, recombination frequencies obtained from single spore data were multiplied by 100 to yield genetic map distances (cM). The recombination frequency in single spores determined by: Parental/(Parental+Recombinant) and cM indicates the genetic distance in tetrads calculated using the formula of Perkins [38]: 50x{TT+(6xNPD)}/(PD+TT+NPD).
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 10 14 10 14 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Oh1">[36]</xref>
###xml 31 44 31 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1&#916;C795</italic>
###xml 389 402 365 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1&#916;C795</italic>
###xml 447 456 419 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 507 516 475 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2-LYS2</italic>
###xml 606 615 574 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 722 731 686 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1025 1034 985 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1034 1038 990 994 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Oh1">[36]</xref>
###xml 1050 1059 1006 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1069 1078 1021 1030 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 1084 1094 1036 1046 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2C</xref>
Oh et al. [36] showed that the sgs1DeltaC795 mutation conferred an approximately20% increase of map distance in SK1 strains that was primarily due to an increase in the frequency of NPD tetrads. Based on this observation the authors suggested "em leader that a fraction of the events that would normally form single crossovers in WT cells gives rise to closely spaced double crossovers in sgs1DeltaC795 cells." We did not see a similar pattern in csm4Delta mutants. Three of four genetic intervals (all but LEU2-LYS2) in the SK1 congenic strain displayed significantly different PD:NPD:TT distributions in csm4Delta compared to WT, even when the NPD class was ignored (G-test, p<0.05). This observation suggested that the csm4Delta mutation did not increase map distances by specifically increasing the frequency of closely spaced double crossovers. This conclusion is reinforced by physical analysis of DNA events: species representing large joint molecules are overrepresented relative to other types of joint molecules in sgs1Delta[36] but not in csm4Delta (compare Figure 7C with Figure S2C).
###end p 51
###begin title 52
###xml 34 43 34 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
Reduced Crossover Interference in csm4Delta
###end title 52
###begin p 53
###xml 217 226 217 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
In WT meiosis, occurrence of a CO in one region of a chromosome is accompanied by a reduced probability that one will also occur in a nearby region, a phenomenon known as "CO interference". We assayed interference in csm4Delta by three different methods.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 51 55 51 55 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Malkova1">[37]</xref>
###xml 193 201 193 201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 203 211 203 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s007">Table S3</xref>
###xml 290 299 290 295 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 511 520 507 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
One approach utilizes the method of Malkova et al. [37], which evaluates the occurrence of interference in adjacent intervals by utilizing all of the information contained in complete tetrads (Figure 4, Table S3). In WT, interference was observed for all three interval pairs. In contrast, csm4Delta strains showed reduced interference in two intervals and no significant interference in the third. One interpretation of these data is that interference does not extend as far from the initial crossover site in csm4Delta strains as it does in WT.
###end p 54
###begin title 55
###xml 49 58 49 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
Crossover interference is partially disrupted in csm4Delta strains on chromosome XV.
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 67 71 67 71 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Malkova1">[37]</xref>
###xml 91 95 91 95 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Martini1">[34]</xref>
###xml 160 167 160 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t001">Table 1</xref>
Crossover interference was analyzed as described by Malkova et al. [37] and Martini et al. [34] using data obtained from the EAY1108/EAY1112 strain background (Table 1). The numbers above the solid arcs are the average of the significance interference ratios for each interval pair. n.s. and dashed arc indicates that both members of the interval pair did not show significant interference.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 292 296 292 296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Malkova1">[37]</xref>
###xml 309 318 309 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 403 410 399 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t002">Table 2</xref>
A second approach evaluated the "coefficient of coincidence" (COC). For a given pair of intervals, the COC is the ratio of the observed frequency of double CO events to that expected if COs in the two intervals occurred independently. In accord with results obtained using the Malkova et al. [37] method, the csm4Delta mutant exhibited a modest reduction in interference in all four intervals analyzed (Table 2).
###end p 57
###begin title 58
###xml 20 29 20 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 31 40 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 42 51 34 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 57 66 45 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
Interference in WT, csm4Delta, ndj1Delta, msh5Delta, and mlh1Delta strains.
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 51 58 51 58 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 528 529 528 529 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">*</sup>
###xml 538 540 538 540 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">**</sup>
###xml 550 553 550 553 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">***</sup>
Interference was calculated from data presented in Table 1. The coefficient of coincidence (COC) was examined by a two-tail binomial test from VassarStats () which tested whether the observed number of double crossovers (DCOs) deviated significantly from the expected number. The expected number of non-parental ditypes (NPDs) and the presence or absence of interference was determined using the two-factor test from the Stahl Laboratory Online Tools website (). Asterisks indicate that interference is present in the interval (* p<0.05; ** p<0.01). ***In this interval, although DCOs deviated significantly from the expected number, the COC is greater than 1.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 252 256 252 256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Perkins1">[38]</xref>
###xml 257 261 257 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Papazian1">[39]</xref>
###xml 355 364 355 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 398 405 394 401 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 487 496 483 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 843 847 835 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Malkova1">[37]</xref>
###xml 848 852 840 844 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Zhao1">[40]</xref>
###xml 882 891 874 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 989 1003 977 991 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3-LYS2-HIS3</italic>
###xml 837 842 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
A third approach to interference analysis is the calculation of the ratio of observed non-parental ditypes (NPD) which reflects the occurrence of a four-strand double crossover, to that predicted by the number of single crossovers detected (NPD ratio, [38],[39]). By this criterion, we were unable to determine a difference in interference between WT and csm4Delta in all three intervals measured (Table 2). It is not clear why interference as assessed by NPD ratios is less affected by csm4Delta than when assessed by other methods. One possible explanation for the disparity between the COC and NPD ratio measurements is that NPD measurements may be affected by "chromatid interference". Chromatid interference is a restriction on the independence of chromatid selection during CO recombination and has not been previously observed in yeast [37],[40]. Correspondingly, WT and the csm4Delta mutant both exhibited a 1:2:1 ratio of exchanges involving two, three, or four chromatids in the URA3-LYS2-HIS3 interval, implying an absence of chromatid interference in both cases (data not shown).
###end p 60
###begin title 61
CSM4 and Crossover-Promoting Factors Act Independently
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 257 261 257 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Brner1">[41]</xref>
###xml 358 362 358 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Franklin1">[42]</xref>
###xml 363 367 363 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Wang1">[44]</xref>
###xml 417 436 417 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 441 460 433 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 574 583 558 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 631 639 611 619 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 641 648 621 628 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 808 817 788 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 822 831 798 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
###xml 920 929 892 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 934 943 902 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
###xml 989 998 953 958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1050 1059 1010 1015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1064 1073 1020 1025 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1096 1105 1048 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1182 1191 1130 1139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3-LEU2</italic>
###xml 1227 1236 1175 1180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1284 1303 1228 1239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1502 1510 1438 1446 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1512 1531 1448 1459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1539 1558 1467 1478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1619 1627 1539 1547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1629 1638 1549 1554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1646 1655 1562 1567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh5&#916;</italic>
###xml 1663 1672 1575 1580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mlh1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1810 1819 1718 1727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4 msh4</italic>
###xml 1845 1849 1753 1757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Kosaka1">[23]</xref>
During meiosis, the formation of COs, as opposed to noncrossovers (NCOs), is promoted by a large number of proteins that are specifically dedicated to this process. Among these, the Msh4-Msh5 complex appears to act around the time of CO/NCO differentiation [41], while Mlh1-Mlh3 appears to act later, likely during double Holliday junction (dHJ) resolution ([42]-[44]; N. Hunter, personal communication). In both the msh5Delta csm4Delta and mlh1Delta csm4Delta double mutants, recombination levels are significantly lower at all examined intervals than levels seen with the csm4Delta alone (G-test, p<0.007, Dunn-Sidak correction, Figure 3, Table 1). This suggests that, while absence of Csm4 affects the level of COs, those COs are still occurring via the normal Msh5/Mlh1-dependent pathway. Conversely, in msh5Delta and mlh1Delta mutant backgrounds, absence of Csm4 increases CO levels about two-fold above the single msh5Delta and mlh1Delta mutant levels, suggesting that the effect of csm4Delta on CO levels is upstream and/or independent of the msh5Delta and mlh1Delta effects. Although the msh5Delta is only significantly different from its corresponding double mutant at the URA3-LEU2 interval in the spore dataset, the mlh1Delta recombination levels differ significantly from mlh1Delta csm4Delta at two out of four intervals in the tetrad dataset and three out of four intervals in the spore dataset (G-test, p<0.025, Dunn-Sidak correction). Furthermore, spore viability in the double mutants (Figure 1; csm4Delta msh5Delta = 22%; mlh1Delta csm4Delta = 42%) was much lower than any of the single mutants alone (Figure 1; csm4Delta = 64%; msh5Delta = 36%; mlh1Delta = 68%). Taken together, these genetic interactions suggest that Csm4 acts independently of Msh4-Msh5 and Mlh1-Mlh3. Physical analysis of csm4 msh4 mutants by Kosaka et al. [23] is consistent with this observation.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
Ndj1 and Csm4 Have the Same Function(s) for CO Level and Distribution
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 0 9 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 118 127 114 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 223 232 215 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 237 246 225 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 430 449 414 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 679 688 655 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 693 712 665 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 770 779 734 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 803 811 763 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 813 820 773 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 851 859 811 819 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 861 868 821 828 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 939 948 899 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 988 992 944 948 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Chua1">[11]</xref>
ndj1Delta conferred a 30-40% increase in CO frequencies at all intervals, indistinguishable from the increase seen in csm4Delta (G-test, p<0.007, Dunn-Sidak correction). Crossover interference is also similarly affected in ndj1Delta and csm4Delta. These unusual phenotypes in both mutants provide strong support for Ndj1 and Csm4 playing similar roles with respect to recombination. In direct confirmation of this conclusion, the csm4Delta ndj1Delta double mutant is indistinguishable from either single mutant with respect to increases in CO levels in all four genetic intervals analyzed (G-test, p<0.017, Dunn-Sidak correction, no intervals are significantly different between csm4Delta and csm4Delta ndj1Delta and only one interval is significantly different between ndj1Delta and the double mutant, Figure 3, Table 1) and interference phenotypes (Figure 4; Table 2). We note that a previous study also detected reduced interference in ndj1Delta but did not detect increased CO levels [11]. Strain background effects are likely responsible for this difference.
###end p 64
###begin title 65
###xml 74 81 74 81 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-1000188-t003">Table 3</xref>
Absence of Csm4 Does Not Dramatically Increase Non-Mendelian Segregation (Table 3)
###end title 65
###begin p 66
###xml 303 307 303 307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Mortimer1">[45]</xref>
###xml 367 371 367 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRP1</italic>
###xml 373 377 373 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 379 383 379 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 385 389 385 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LYS2</italic>
###xml 391 395 391 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ADE1</italic>
###xml 401 405 401 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS3</italic>
###xml 505 514 505 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 802 806 798 802 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-delosSantos1">[46]</xref>
###xml 908 917 904 909 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1014 1023 1006 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1408 1417 1396 1401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 193 198 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Non-Mendelian (non-2:2) segregation of an allele, often referred to as "gene conversion", implies that a recombination interaction has occurred between homologs rather than sisters. In budding yeast, gene conversion events are usually manifested as 1:3 or 3:1 segregation patterns of individual alleles [45]. In the congenic SK1 background, gene conversion levels at TRP1, URA3, LEU2, LYS2, ADE1, and HIS3 loci occurred at levels ranging from 0 to 0.8% of tetrads in WT and at indistinguishable levels in csm4Delta. The relatively low levels of gene conversion observed for these markers may reflect the fact that they mostly involve 1-3 kb heterologies. We also examined gene conversion at 11 loci marked by a variety of mutation types (point mutations and insertions/deletions). In these SK1 strains [46], non-Mendelian segregation frequencies ranged from 0.2% to 5.3% of tetrads in WT and 0.2% to 5.2% in csm4Delta derivatives. The total frequencies of gene conversion at all loci were 14.7% in WT and 17.4% in csm4Delta, with no chromosome- or locus-specific differences detectable. Gene conversion frequencies reflect the combined effects of a couple of variables: the frequency of recombination initiation at/near the locus and the probability that an event initiated on one homolog will chose a partner duplex on the other homolog rather than on the sister chromatid. The simplest possibility is that csm4Delta has little effect on either of these features, although a balanced effect on both parameters cannot be excluded.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
###xml 0 9 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
csm4Delta does not significantly affect the percentage of non-mendelian segregation events observed in tetrads.
###end title 67
###begin p 68
Percentage of gene conversion events on chromosome XV in the EAY1108/EAY1112 SK1 congenic background. Of the 167 aberrant segregation events detected, 161 were 3:1 or 1:3 single gene conversions and 6 were 4:0 or 0:4 double gene conversions. No post-meiotic segregation events were detected.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
Gene conversion percentage on chromosomes III, VII, and VIII in the NH942/NH943 SK1 isogenic background. Of the 169 aberrant segregation events detected, 168 were 3:1 or 1:3 single gene conversions and 1 was a 4:0 or 0:4 double gene conversion. No post-meiotic segregation events were detected.
###end p 69
###begin title 70
###xml 26 35 26 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
Homolog Nondisjunction in csm4Delta Does Not Result from Absence of the Obligatory CO
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 387 396 387 392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 485 494 481 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 739 743 731 735 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Martini1">[34]</xref>
Homolog disjunction requires the presence of at least one interhomolog connection, created by the combined effects of a CO and the cohesion between sister chromatids centromere-distal to that CO. Homolog disjunction also requires appropriate reductional functioning of homolog centromere/kinetochore complexes and the efficient release of chiasma-maintaining sister connections. Because csm4Delta exhibits higher than WT levels of COs, it seems unlikely that homolog nondisjunction in csm4Delta results from the absence of a CO. On the other hand, in WT meiosis, special mechanisms ensure that each homolog pair experiences at least one CO (the so-called "obligatory" CO) even when overall CO levels are reduced (for recent discussion see [34]). Thus, it remained possible that Csm4 is required for the occurrence of the obligatory CO.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 137 141 137 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Rockmill2">[29]</xref>
###xml 143 151 143 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 153 161 153 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s008">Table S4</xref>
###xml 303 311 303 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s005">Table S1</xref>
###xml 313 334 313 334 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 572 581 572 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 720 729 716 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 790 799 782 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 929 938 917 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
We examined the presence or absence of COs on chromosomes that had undergone nondisjunction using a system developed by Rockmill et al. ([29]; Figure 5, Table S4). This system allows for the selection, purification, and genetic analysis of spores disomic for chromosome III in the BR strain background (Table S1, Materials and Methods). As a baseline for this analysis, map distances for six intervals spanning 167 kb of the 317 kb chromosome III were determined from four-spore viable tetrads in WT (390 tetrads dissected, 317 four-spore-viable, 93% spore viability) and csm4Delta (697 tetrads dissected, 203 four-spore viable, 53% spore viability) in the BR strain background. This spore viability pattern observed in csm4Delta was similar to that seen for both the congenic and isogenic csm4Delta SK1 strains. However, unlike what we observed in the SK1 strain background, the recombination frequencies were similar in WT and csm4Delta (only two out of six intervals were significantly different, G-test, p<0.025, Dunn-Sidak correction, see comment on strain background effects below).
###end p 72
###begin title 73
###xml 63 72 63 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
An altered distribution and frequency of crossovers is seen in csm4Delta cells that have suffered a chromosome III nondisjunction event.
###end title 73
###begin p 74
###xml 73 94 73 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 153 162 153 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 175 184 171 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 214 222 206 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s008">Table S4</xref>
###xml 557 566 549 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 675 684 663 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
A) Cartoon showing the chromosome III locus in the BR strain background (Materials and Methods). B) Graphical representation of recombination for WT and csm4Delta tetrads and csm4Delta disomic spores (from data in Table S4). Error bars indicate 95% confidence intervals around the recombination frequency determined from single spores, calculated using VassarStats (). "i" indicates insertion of the indicated marker at an ectopic locus. Recombination frequencies obtained from single spore data were multiplied by 100 to yield genetic map distances (cM). *csm4Delta disomic recombination levels are significantly different (G-test, p <0.025, Dunn-Sidak correction) from the csm4Delta tetrad data.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 23 32 23 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 311 320 307 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 589 598 581 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
Tetrad analysis of the csm4Delta derivatives of these strains showed that 9.3% (17/182) of the two-spore-viable tetrads dissected displayed nondisjunction of chromosome III. This value is similar to what was seen in the congenic SK1 strain background (7.8%). Tetrad analysis also revealed that 85% (154/182) of csm4Delta two-spore-viable tetrads were sisters, consistent with meiosis I nondisjunction, and again, similar to that seen in the congenic SK1 strain background (88%). These data, along with the spore viability profile (data not shown), show that again, aberrant segregation in csm4Delta strains resulted primarily from homolog nondisjunction.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 16 25 16 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 244 253 240 245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 394 415 386 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 606 615 598 603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 625 634 613 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 691 701 675 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">iNAT-iLEU2</italic>
###xml 706 715 690 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">iLEU2-MAT</italic>
###xml 821 831 805 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4-iTHR1</italic>
###xml 880 888 864 872 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 890 898 874 882 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s008">Table S4</xref>
###xml 1039 1048 1023 1028 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1075 1083 1055 1063 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 1085 1093 1065 1073 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s008">Table S4</xref>
###xml 1128 1137 1108 1113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
From sporulated csm4Delta cultures, we selected and analyzed 185 random spores disomic for chromosome III. In this analysis, CO levels were examined in a manner that accounted for the inability to detect homozygosity of dominant markers in the csm4Delta disomic spores and all tetrad information was converted to single spore data to allow direct comparison between the disome and tetrad data (Materials and Methods). Interestingly, the distribution of COs among the examined intervals was significantly different from that observed among chromosomes that experienced regular segregation: when compared to csm4Delta tetrads, csm4Delta disomes displayed significantly increased levels in the iNAT-iLEU2 and iLEU2-MAT intervals on the right arm of the chromosome and a significantly decreased level of crossing over in the HIS4-iTHR1 region (G-test, p<0.025, Dunn-Sidak correction, Figure 5, Table S4). In addition, the total map distance for six intervals on chromosome III was higher for the disomes (85 cM) compared to the WT (78 cM) and csm4Delta (71 cM) complete tetrads (Figure 5, Table S4). Thus, homolog nondisjunction in csm4Delta does not appear to result from absence of the obligatory CO.
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 277 286 277 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 371 380 367 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1&#916;</italic>
###xml 614 618 606 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Rockmill2">[29]</xref>
###xml 636 640 628 632 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Rockmill2">[29]</xref>
###xml 719 728 711 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1&#916;</italic>
###xml 883 892 871 876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1327 1337 1311 1321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
More generally, chromosomes are not mis-segregating because of lack of recombination events, too many recombination events, or because they were only receiving crossovers in inappropriate locations (e.g., telomeres, centromeres). The altered distribution of crossovers seen in csm4Delta disomes also differed from what was previously seen in disomes isolated from WT and sgs1Delta strains. In these backgrounds, elevated levels of crossing over were seen at all loci with the highest levels found at those closest to the centromere, consistent with PSSC causing the majority of the mis-segregation events detected [29]. Rockmill et al. [29] hypothesized that the increase in centromere-proximal crossing over in WT and sgs1Delta strains caused PSSC events through the loss of sister chromatid cohesion. However, our data are not consistent with this scenario. The crossovers seen in csm4Delta disomes were not consistently higher or lower across the chromosome length, were not localized to a specific chromosomal position (e.g. centromeres), and were clearly not aiding in proper chromosome segregation. Thus there is no clear pattern or trend from these data that can explain how such a changed distribution can cause chromosome mis-segregation. A different type of explanation for homolog nondisjunction is presented below (Discussion).
###end p 77
###begin title 78
Physical Analysis of Recombination
###end title 78
###begin p 79
###xml 42 61 42 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;/ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 166 174 158 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 200 209 192 201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 458 461 450 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cis</italic>
###xml 538 546 530 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 720 730 712 722 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s003">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 784 792 776 784 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s005">Table S1</xref>
To address the nature of recombination in csm4Delta/ndj1Delta meiosis in more detail, we assayed, in synchronously initiated meiotic cultures, physical events at the HIS4LEU2 locus of chromosome III (Figure 6A), where virtually all events emanate from a single DSB hot spot. Since Csm4 and Ndj1 are implicated in telomere status and dynamics (below), we also asked whether mutant recombination phenotypes depend upon the presence of chromosomal telomeres in cis to the assayed locus. For many phenotypes we analyzed recombination between HIS4LEU2 loci present on circular versions of chromosome III as well as on normal linear chromosomes III. Presence of the circular chromosome was confirmed for all analyzed strains (Figure S3A). All strains examined are isogenic SK1 derivatives (Table S1).
###end p 79
###begin title 80
###xml 34 42 34 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 50 59 50 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>

###xml 76 95 68 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>

###xml 277 286 277 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2.</italic>
###xml 329 332 329 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 413 420 413 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 426 429 426 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bam</italic>
###xml 564 575 564 575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50S-KI81</italic>

The locations of the relevant XhoI (X), parental, and DSB sites are indicated. B, C) 2D gel analysis of CO and NCO products at HIS4LEU2. B 2D gel of CO and NCO tester constructs. ###end p 81
###begin title 82
High Levels of DSBs and CO/NCO Products
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 125 134 125 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 136 140 136 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Martini1">[34]</xref>
###xml 165 174 165 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 176 185 172 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 191 210 183 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 265 274 249 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6C</xref>
###xml 369 375 353 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50S</italic>
###xml 387 391 371 375 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Alani1">[47]</xref>
###xml 448 457 432 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6D</xref>
###xml 462 465 446 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s003">S3B</xref>
###xml 686 694 670 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 696 705 680 689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6C</xref>
###xml 716 725 700 709 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 849 857 833 841 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 875 879 859 863 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Kosaka1">[23]</xref>
The levels of CO and noncrossover (NCO) products were determined at the end of meiosis using a two-dimensional gel approach (Figure 6B; [34]). In all three mutants (ndj1Delta, csm4Delta, and ndj1Delta csm4Delta), both types of products were present at high levels (Figure 6C). Correspondingly, DSBs form at the very similar levels in all four strains, as assessed in a rad50S background [47] where their turnover to later intermediates is blocked (Figure 6D and S3B). Genetic analysis (above) detected modest increases in COs and non-Mendelian segregations, which presumptively represent total events and thus NCOs as well as COs. Such increases are not obvious in the present study at HIS4LEU2 (Figure 6C; see also Figure 7C "COs"); however, slightly increased levels of DSBs are reported from analogous analysis of a slightly different version of HIS4LEU2 by Kosaka et al. [23].
###end p 83
###begin title 84
###xml 34 42 34 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 50 59 50 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 61 70 57 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 76 95 68 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>
Meiotic recombination analysis at HIS4LEU2 in WT, csm4Delta, ndj1Delta, and csm4Delta ndj1Delta, Part II.
###end title 84
###begin p 85
###xml 60 69 60 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 71 80 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 86 105 78 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 276 284 260 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 289 299 273 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leu2::hisG</italic>
###xml 305 309 289 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Oh1">[36]</xref>
###xml 663 672 647 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 674 683 654 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 689 708 665 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 971 992 939 960 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 1190 1199 1158 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1205 1224 1169 1180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916; ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1238 1246 1194 1202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 1256 1265 1212 1221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
A, B) DNA physical analysis of meiotic recombination in WT, csm4Delta, ndj1Delta, and csm4Delta ndj1Delta. A Synchronous meiotic cultures of the indicated WT and mutant strains analyzed by 1D Southern blot. "Ects" are DNA signal resulting from ectopic recombination involving HIS4LEU2 and leu2::hisG (see [36]). B) 2D gel analysis of recombination intermediates isolated from the indicated WT and mutant strains at times following meiotic induction; same cultures as in A. The positions of single end invasions (SEIs) and double Holliday junctions (dHJs) are indicated by a fork line in the left panel. C) Kinetics of meiotic recombination and MI division in WT, csm4Delta, ndj1Delta, and csm4Delta ndj1Delta containing linear (NKY3890-3893) or circular chromosome III (NKY3894-3897). Levels of DSBs, SEIs, dHJs, and COs are shown for each time point sample as percentages of total DNA. Occurrence of MI shown as percentage of cells that have completed MI (assayed as in Materials and Methods) regardless of whether they have or have not also completed later steps. D) Lifespans of all three assayed intermediates in the two experiments shown in A-C and in a third experiment involving WT, csm4Delta, and csm4Delta ndj1Delta for the same HIS4LEU2 alleles (Figure 6A) but a slightly different strain background. E) Analysis of the effects of analyzed mutations on inter-event intervals. For each strain analyzed, a cumulative curve was calculated for entry into the DSB, SEI and dHJ stages, and COs and MI were plotted as % of their maximum levels. From each of these plots, the time at which 50% of cells had "entered the stage" was determined. Then, for each pair of successive events, the interval between the corresponding 50% points was determined. Finally, for each strain examined, and for each such interval, the difference between the interval in the mutant and the interval in WT was determined and plotted.
###end p 85
###begin title 86
Delays at Every Post-DSB Step of Recombination
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 0 6 0 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50S</italic>
###xml 197 206 197 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g006">Figure 6D</xref>
###xml 282 286 282 286 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Borde1">[48]</xref>
rad50S data also show that DSBs occur in a timely fashion in all three mutants, with small differences in timing among different strains that are well within standard culture-to-culture variation (Figure 6D). Since the timing of DSB formation reflects the timing of DNA replication [48] this suggests that DNA replication also occurs with normal timing, which we have confirmed directly in all three mutants by FACS analysis (data not shown).
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 398 402 398 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Bishop1">[49]</xref>
###xml 403 407 403 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Allers1">[50]</xref>
###xml 408 412 408 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Hunter1">[51]</xref>
###xml 414 429 414 429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7A and B</xref>
###xml 431 441 431 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s003">Figure S3C</xref>
###xml 647 656 647 656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 910 919 910 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 1133 1149 1133 1149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2A and B</xref>
After DSB formation, however, progression through ensuing steps of recombination is severely delayed, for both linear and circular chromosomes. These steps were analyzed by one-dimensional gels that display DSBs and CO products plus two-dimensional gels that display single-end invasions (SEIs) and double Holliday junctions (dHJs), two branched species on the pathway to formation of CO products ([49],[50],[51]; Figure 7A and B; Figure S3C). All three intermediates (DSBs, SEIs, and dHJs) occur at higher than normal levels and peak at later than normal times in all three mutants, with very similar results for linear and circular chromosomes (Figure 7C). This pattern is indicative of delayed progression, as discussed in detail below. Correspondingly, while CO products form at high levels in all cases, they appear with a substantial delay in all three mutants, for both linear and circular chromosomes (Figure 7C). An additional type of one-dimensional gel analysis of the linear chromosome strains reveals that the same is also true for NCO products, which are delayed to the same extent as CO products in all three mutants (Figure S2A and B).
###end p 88
###begin p 89
###xml 24 43 24 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;/csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 157 161 149 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Hunter1">[51]</xref>
###xml 611 620 603 612 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7D</xref>
The detailed effects of ndj1Delta/csm4Delta mutations on recombination progression are elucidated by further analysis of the primary data, by two approaches [51]. First, the lifespan of an intermediate, given by the area under the corresponding primary data curve, defines the time spent by a given intermediate at that stage; thus, an increase in the lifespan of a species implies a delay in progression out of the corresponding step. The lifespans of DSBs, dHJs and SEIs all increased in each of the three mutants, relative to WT, for both linear and circular chromosomes, with the biggest increase for DSBs (Figure 7D). Thus, all three mutants confer defects in all three corresponding steps, with the biggest delay in progression out of the DSB stage and lesser delays in progression from SEIs to dHJs and progression from dHJs to COs.
###end p 89
###begin p 90
###xml 786 795 786 795 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7E</xref>
###xml 900 909 900 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 1000 1015 1000 1015 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7D and E</xref>
###xml 1115 1124 1115 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1124 1128 1120 1124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Wu1">[16]</xref>
Second, cumulative curve analysis defines the percentage of cells that have "entered" a particular stage as a function of time after initiation of meiosis, with "time of entry" defined as the time at which 50% of cells have carried out the corresponding step. Once again, a delay in progression is seen as an increase in the time interval between the entry time for one step and the entry time for the successive step. Among the three transitions examined, the biggest effect of the mutations is on the difference between the time of DSB formation and the time of SEI formation (i.e. the DSB-to-SEI transition), as expected from lifespan analysis, with smaller (or no) differences seen for the other two other transitions (SEI formation to dHJ formation, dHJ formation to CO formation; Figure 7E). We note that similar effects have been observed not only in the two complete experiments presented in Figure 7C but in a third set of experiments involving a different set of linear chromosome strains (Figure 7D and E, "Lin2"). We also note that while previous work suggested no delay in the DSB-to-SEI transition in ndj1Delta[16], reanalysis of that data suggests that the same delay was observed in that study as is reported here.
###end p 90
###begin p 91
###xml 492 501 492 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 570 585 566 581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7D and E</xref>
We conclude that: (i) absence of Ndj1 and/or Csm4 confers delayed progression at every individual assayable step of recombination but most prominently at the DSB to SEI transition; (ii) that linear and circular chromosomes behave quite similarly with respect to these effects, though minor differences are not excluded; and (iii) that delays are not accompanied by any significant reduction (or obvious increase) in the level of final CO and NCO products. There is also a strong tendency for csm4Delta to confer the strongest effects among the three analyzed mutations (Figure 7D and E).
###end p 91
###begin p 92
###xml 11 20 11 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1/csm4</italic>
###xml 132 148 132 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2C and D</xref>
###xml 233 237 233 237 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Oh1">[36]</xref>
###xml 248 257 248 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1/csm4</italic>
###xml 284 294 284 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2C</xref>
###xml 503 513 503 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2D</xref>
###xml 515 519 515 519 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Oh1">[36]</xref>
###xml 599 603 599 603 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LEU2</italic>
###xml 613 621 613 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 641 645 641 645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">leu2</italic>
###xml 652 656 652 656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Grushcow1">[52]</xref>
###xml 754 764 754 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2C</xref>
###xml 798 807 798 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 807 811 803 807 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Goldman1">[18]</xref>
###xml 1010 1020 982 992 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2C</xref>
###xml 1156 1160 1128 1132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Schwacha1">[53]</xref>
###xml 1527 1537 1499 1509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s002">Figure S2C</xref>
Effects of ndj1/csm4 mutations on three other aspects of recombination were also examined for both linear and circular chromosomes (Figure S2C and D). First, "large joint molecules" (LJMs), indicative of multi-chromatid interactions [36], occur in ndj1/csm4 mutants as in WT meiosis (Figure S2C). Moreover, direct comparison of LJM and dHJ levels reveals that the two species are affected coordinately, with no indication that the mutants have increased LJM levels as observed in certain other mutants (Figure S2D; [36]). Second, ectopic recombination, which occurs between the molecularly-inserted LEU2 locus at HIS4LEU2 and the endogenous leu2 locus [52], is slightly elevated in all three mutants, as compared to WT, as seen at very late time points (Figure S2C), and as previously observed for ndj1Delta[18]. Third, for the linear chromosome, all three mutants exhibit a significant, but somewhat reduced, ratio of inter-homolog versus inter-sister dHJs (approximately2.7:1 versus approximately5:1 for WT; Figure S2C). This difference could reflect: (i) defective homolog partner choice at the time that choice is made (concomitant with DSB formation; [53], K.K. and N.K. unpublished); (ii) deterioration of homolog bias thereafter; and/or (iii) a differential role of Ndj1/Csm4 in progression of inter-homolog CO interactions versus inter-sister CO interactions. No such difference is observed for the circular chromosome; perhaps this is related to the fact that it does not exhibit such strong inter-homolog bias in WT (Figure S2C).
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 68 77 68 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 95 99 91 95 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Kosaka1">[23]</xref>
###xml 384 392 380 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
We note that related analysis of linear chromosome recombination in csm4Delta by Kosaka et al. [23] also reveals delays at all assayable steps, very similar to the delays reported here, and, coordinately, delays in formation of COs and NCOs. The two studies differ somewhat with respect to reported effects on the levels of COs and NCOs, perhaps because slightly different assays and HIS4LEU2 alleles were used. However, in both cases, high levels of both products do occur.
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Recombination-Dependent MI Delay
###end title 94
###begin p 95
###xml 10 19 10 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1/csm4</italic>
###xml 109 118 109 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 133 142 129 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 295 304 287 296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 438 441 430 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Koszul1">[6]</xref>
###xml 442 446 434 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Wu1">[16]</xref>
###xml 605 624 597 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;/csm4&#916;</italic>
All three ndj1/csm4 mutations confer delays in the occurrence of MI. The extent of the delay is greatest for csm4Delta, smallest for ndj1Delta, and intermediate for the double mutant. This is a highly reproducible effect. It has been observed in both linear and circular chromosome experiments (Figure 7C) and in all of the many other experiments performed with these mutants in the current and previous studies using the SK1 background ([6],[16]; data not shown). In a number of mutants, delayed and/or inefficient occurrence of MI results from delayed recombinational progression. This is also true for ndj1Delta/csm4Delta mutants: elimination of recombination initiation completely eliminates the MI delay in all three mutant strains (see below).
###end p 95
###begin p 96
###xml 457 466 457 462 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 545 554 541 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7D</xref>
###xml 848 856 844 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIS4LEU2</italic>
###xml 1031 1041 1027 1037 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
Appearance of COs and NCOs marks the end of recombination. Since MI delays are due to delays in recombination, it might be expected that, once these products appear, the mutants should exhibit no further delay in progression. Specifically: occurrence of MI should be delayed to the same extent as occurrence of COs. However, there are hints that this is not the case: occurrence of MI is even further delayed than is occurrence of COs, dramatically for two csm4Delta experiments and less dramatically for other mutants and/or other experiments (Figure 7D). Moreover, since all MI delays are completely dependent upon recombination initiation (below), this discrepancy seems to imply that, even after the majority of recombinational interactions are completed (as seen by appearance of the high levels of COs and NCOs as detected by DNA analysis at HIS4LEU2), a minority of interactions (which do not make a significant contribution to total DNA-detected events) remain unresolved and are either completed much later or not at all (Discussion).
###end p 96
###begin p 97
###xml 74 82 74 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 98 119 98 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g008">Figure 8B, left panel</xref>
###xml 199 204 199 204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spo11</italic>
###xml 205 210 205 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Y153F</italic>
###xml 222 244 222 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g008">Figure 8B, right panel</xref>
###xml 270 279 270 275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 279 283 275 279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Wu1">[16]</xref>
###xml 292 301 288 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 319 323 311 315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Kosaka1">[23]</xref>
###xml 444 448 436 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Brner1">[41]</xref>
###xml 449 453 441 445 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Bishop2">[54]</xref>
###xml 460 469 452 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 530 540 518 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad17&#916;</italic>
###xml 551 560 535 544 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000188.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 665 674 649 654 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 676 680 656 660 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Wu2">[55]</xref>
###xml 702 722 682 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad17&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 893 897 865 869 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Wu2">[55]</xref>
###xml 898 902 870 874 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Lydall1">[56]</xref>
We further find that the delays in occurrence of MI in all three mutants (Figure 7, also shown in Figure 8B, left panel) are completely eliminated if initiation of recombination is eliminated by the spo11(Y153F) mutation (Figure 8B, right panel), as seen previously for ndj1Delta[16] and for csm4Delta by Kosaka et al. [23]. This effect is in accord with the fact that recombination defects trigger MI defects in several other situations (e.g. [41],[54]). For csm4Delta we further determined that the MI delay was eliminated by a rad17Delta mutation (Figure S4), which is known to alleviate MI delays resulting from recombinational blocks in other situations (e.g. ndj1Delta; [55]). Spore viability in rad17Delta csm4Delta was dramatically reduced as compared to either single mutant, as would be expected from the compromise of a checkpoint that monitors aberrant recombinational progression [55],[56].
###end p 97
###begin title 98
###xml 50 59 50 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 60 69 56 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
Synaptonemal complex formation and sporulation in ndj1Delta/csm4Delta mutants.
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 192 195 192 195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Scherthan1">[2]</xref>
###xml 196 199 196 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Koszul1">[6]</xref>
###xml 490 499 490 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 501 520 497 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 526 535 514 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 854 855 838 839 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</underline>
###xml 1011 1021 995 1001 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;,</italic>
###xml 1026 1035 1006 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1183 1192 1159 1164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1340 1349 1312 1317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1351 1370 1319 1330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1376 1385 1336 1341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1609 1618 1565 1570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1623 1632 1575 1580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 1733 1744 1681 1692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spo11-Y135F</italic>
A) Meiotic progression, as measured by the formation of synaptonemal complex (SC). Meiotic progression was monitored in strains where the SC was illuminated by Zip1-GFP(700) (for details, see [2],[6]). i The various steps of SC formation are shown for a WT strain (NKY3834): after diffuse fluorescence, dots appear that correspond to formation of DSBs. Later, short lines correspond to the zygotene onset, whereas at the pachytene stage SC appears as linear, contiguous ribbons. ii For WT, ndj1Delta, ndj1Delta csm4Delta, and csm4Delta strains (NKY3834, NKY3837, NKY4003, and NKY4002, respectively), fixed nuclei where examined at hourly intervals and scored for zygotene (triangle symbol) or pachytene (square symbol) categories. The proportions of nuclei within one or the other categories are plotted as a function of time in SPM. Completion of MI (MI+MII) for each time course is indicated by a dotted line curve. iii zygotene and pachytene lifespan as deduced from the cumulative curve analysis for WT and ndj1Delta, and csm4Delta mutants. iv Cumulative curve analysis of zygotene and pachytene progression. The upper two panels indicate zygotene and pachytene for WT (top) and csm4Delta (bottom). The lower two panels show the onset of zygotene (top) and pachytene (bottom) for all strains. Color code is the same as in ii. v For WT, ndj1Delta, ndj1Delta csm4Delta, and csm4Delta strains, differences between the time when 50% of the nuclei have progressed through MI and the time when 50% have exited pachytene. B) Meiotic progression, as measured by completion of MI divisions in WT (NKY3834), and in ndj1Delta and csm4Delta mutants without (full symbols, upper panel; strains NKY3837 and NKY4002, respectively) and with the spo11-Y135F mutation (empty symbols, lower panel; strains NKY3907 and NKY3908, respectively). All scale bars represent 2 microm.
###end p 99
###begin title 100
SC Morphogenesis
###end title 100
###begin p 101
###xml 99 103 99 103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Brner1">[41]</xref>
###xml 104 108 104 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Brner2">[57]</xref>
###xml 393 402 393 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g008">Figure 8A</xref>
###xml 418 422 418 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000188-Brner2">[57]</xref>
Morphogenesis of the SC is readily monitored in whole cells using Zip1-GFP as described previously [41],[57]: cells containing focal Zip1-GFP are in leptotene; those with an incomplete complement of Zip1 linearities are in zygotene, corresponding to formation of SC; and those containing a maximum complement of Zip1 linearities are in pachytene, a morphology corresponding to full length SC (Figure 8A, panel i; e.g. [57]).
###end p 101
###begin p 102
###xml 0 9 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 11 20 7 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916;</italic>
###xml 26 45 18 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ndj1&#916; csm4&#916;</italic>
###xml 150 159 134 143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000188-g008">Figure 8A</xref>
